      <p><b>Guinea-Bissau</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/aʊ/: 'ou' in 'mouth'">aʊ</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Guinea-Bissau.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/ce/En-us-Guinea-Bissau.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Guinea-Bissau.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <i lang="pt">Guiné-Bissau</i>, <a href="/wiki/Fula_language" title="Fula language">Fula</a>: <i lang="ff-Latn">𞤘𞤭𞤲𞤫 𞤄𞤭𞤧𞤢𞥄𞤱𞤮 Gine-Bisaawo</i>, <a href="/wiki/Mandinka_language" title="Mandinka language">Mandinka</a>: ߖߌߣߍ&nbsp;ߺ ߓߌߛߊߥߏ߫ <i>Gine-Bisawo</i>), officially the <b>Republic of Guinea-Bissau</b> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <i lang="pt">República da Guiné-Bissau</i> <span style="font-size:85%;"></span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">[ʁɛˈpuβlikɐ ðɐ ɣiˈnɛ βiˈsaw]</a></span>), is a country in <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a> that covers 36,125 square kilometres (13,948&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) with an estimated population of 1,874,303.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-4">[4]</a></sup> It borders <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> to <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau%E2%80%93Senegal_border" title="Guinea-Bissau–Senegal border">the north</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a> to <a href="/wiki/Guinea%E2%80%93Guinea-Bissau_border" title="Guinea–Guinea-Bissau border">the south-east</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Guinea-Bissau was once part of the kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Kaabu" title="Kaabu">Kaabu</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-nationsonline.org_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nationsonline.org-8">[8]</a></sup> as well as part of the <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">Mali Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nationsonline.org_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nationsonline.org-8">[8]</a></sup> Parts of this kingdom persisted until the 18th century, while a few others were under some rule by the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> since the 16th century. In the 19th century, it was colonised as <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Guinea" title="Portuguese Guinea">Portuguese Guinea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nationsonline.org_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nationsonline.org-8">[8]</a></sup> Upon independence, declared in 1973 and recognised in 1974, the name of its capital, <a href="/wiki/Bissau" title="Bissau">Bissau</a>, was added to the country's name to prevent confusion with <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/French_Guinea" title="French Guinea">French Guinea</a>). Guinea-Bissau has a history of political instability since independence, and only one elected president (<a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_M%C3%A1rio_Vaz" title="José Mário Vaz">José Mário Vaz</a>) has successfully served a full five-year term.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The current president is <a href="/wiki/Umaro_Sissoco_Embal%C3%B3" title="Umaro Sissoco Embaló">Umaro Sissoco Embaló</a>, who was elected on 29 December 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Only about 2% of the population speaks Portuguese, the official language, as a first language, and 33% speak it as a second language. However, <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_Creole" title="Guinea-Bissau Creole">Creole</a> is the national language and also considered the language of unity. According to a 2012 study, 54% of the population speak Creole as a first language and about 40% speak it as a second language.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> The remainder speak a variety of native African languages. There are diverse religions in Guinea-Bissau. <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> are the main <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Guinea-Bissau" title="Religion in Guinea-Bissau">religions</a> practised in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-cia-religion_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-religion-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-13">[13]</a></sup> The country's per-capita <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">lowest in the world</a>. </p>
      <p>Guinea-Bissau is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Francophonie" class="mw-redirect" title="La Francophonie">La Francophonie</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_Peace_and_Cooperation_Zone" title="South Atlantic Peace and Cooperation Zone">South Atlantic Peace and Cooperation Zone</a>, and was a member of the now-defunct <a href="/wiki/Latin_Union" title="Latin Union">Latin Union</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="History of Guinea-Bissau">History of Guinea-Bissau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Guinea" title="Portuguese Guinea">Portuguese Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Archeology has insufficiently explained the Guinea-Bissau pre-history. In 1000 CE, there were hunter-gatherers in the area, hundreds of thousands of years after they traversed the rest of Africa. This was shortly followed, in the archaeological record by agriculturists, using iron tools.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Guinea-Bissau was once part of the kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Kaabu" title="Kaabu">Kaabu</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">Mali Empire</a> in the 16th century.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Parts of this kingdom persisted until the 18th century. Other parts of the territory in the current country were considered by the Portuguese as part of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">their empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (May 2020)">better&nbsp;source&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Guinea" title="Portuguese Guinea">Portuguese Guinea</a> was known as the <a href="/wiki/Slave_Coast_of_West_Africa" title="Slave Coast of West Africa">Slave Coast</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-HISTORY_OF_GUINEA-BISSAU_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HISTORY_OF_GUINEA-BISSAU-17">[17]</a></sup> as it was a major area for the exportation of African slaves by Europeans to the western hemisphere.<sup id="cite_ref-HISTORY_OF_GUINEA-BISSAU_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HISTORY_OF_GUINEA-BISSAU-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Early reports of Europeans reaching this area include those of the <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venetian</a> <a href="/wiki/Alvise_Cadamosto" title="Alvise Cadamosto">Alvise Cadamosto</a>'s voyage of 1455, the 1479–1480 voyage by Flemish-French trader <a href="/wiki/Eustache_de_la_Fosse" title="Eustache de la Fosse">Eustache de la Fosse</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Diogo_C%C3%A3o" title="Diogo Cão">Diogo Cão</a>. In the 1480s this Portuguese explorer reached the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> and the lands of <a href="/wiki/Bakongo" class="mw-redirect" title="Bakongo">Bakongo</a>, setting up the foundations of modern <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, some 4200&nbsp;km down the African coast from Guinea-Bissau.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Portugueseguineacompanyflag.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Portugueseguineacompanyflag.svg/220px-Portugueseguineacompanyflag.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Portugueseguineacompanyflag.svg/330px-Portugueseguineacompanyflag.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Portugueseguineacompanyflag.svg/440px-Portugueseguineacompanyflag.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1578" data-file-height="1052"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Portugueseguineacompanyflag.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Flag of the Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Company_of_Guinea" class="mw-redirect" title="Company of Guinea">Company of Guinea</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Although the rivers and coast of this area were among the first places colonized by the Portuguese, who set up trading posts in the 16th century, they did not explore the interior until the 19th century. The local African rulers in Guinea, some of whom prospered greatly from the <a href="/wiki/Slave_trade" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave trade">slave trade</a>, controlled the inland trade and did not allow the Europeans into the interior.<sup id="cite_ref-HISTORY_OF_GUINEA-BISSAU_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HISTORY_OF_GUINEA-BISSAU-17">[17]</a></sup> They kept them in the fortified coastal settlements where the trading took place.<sup id="cite_ref-history_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-20">[20]</a></sup> African communities that fought back against slave traders also distrusted European adventurers and would-be settlers. The Portuguese in Guinea were largely restricted to the ports of <a href="/wiki/Bissau" title="Bissau">Bissau</a><sup id="cite_ref-HISTORY_OF_GUINEA-BISSAU_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HISTORY_OF_GUINEA-BISSAU-17">[17]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Cacheu" title="Cacheu">Cacheu</a>. A small number of European settlers established isolated farms along Bissau's inland rivers.<sup id="cite_ref-history_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-20">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>For a brief period in the 1790s, the British tried to establish a rival foothold on an offshore island, at <a href="/wiki/Bolama_Island" title="Bolama Island">Bolama</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> But by the 19th century the Portuguese were sufficiently secure in Bissau to regard the neighbouring coastline as their own special territory,<sup id="cite_ref-HISTORY_OF_GUINEA-BISSAU_17-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HISTORY_OF_GUINEA-BISSAU-17">[17]</a></sup> also up north in part of present South Senegal.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>An <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_War_of_Independence" title="Guinea-Bissau War of Independence">armed rebellion</a>, begun in 1956 by the <a href="/wiki/Partido_Africano_da_Independ%C3%AAncia_da_Guin%C3%A9_e_Cabo_Verde" class="mw-redirect" title="Partido Africano da Independência da Guiné e Cabo Verde">African Party for the Independence of Guinea and Cape Verde</a> (PAIGC) under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%ADlcar_Cabral" title="Amílcar Cabral">Amílcar Cabral</a><sup id="cite_ref-HISTORY_OF_GUINEA-BISSAU_17-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HISTORY_OF_GUINEA-BISSAU-17">[17]</a></sup> gradually consolidated its hold on the then <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Guinea" title="Portuguese Guinea">Portuguese Guinea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Unlike guerrilla movements in other <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese colonies</a>, the PAIGC rapidly extended its military control over large portions of the territory, aided by the jungle-like terrain, its easily reached borderlines with neighbouring allies, and large quantities of arms from <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, and left-leaning African countries.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Cuba also agreed to supply artillery experts, doctors, and technicians.<sup id="cite_ref-Cuba!_Africa!_Revolution!_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cuba!_Africa!_Revolution!-24">[24]</a></sup> The PAIGC even managed to acquire a significant anti-aircraft capability in order to defend itself against aerial attack. By 1973, the PAIGC was in control of many parts of Guinea, although the movement suffered a setback in January 1973 when Cabral was assassinated.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Independence_.281973.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(1973)">Independence (1973)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Independence (1973)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hastear_da_bandeira_da_Guin%C3%A9_Bissau_ap%C3%B3s_o_arrear_da_de_Portugal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Hastear_da_bandeira_da_Guin%C3%A9_Bissau_ap%C3%B3s_o_arrear_da_de_Portugal.jpg/220px-Hastear_da_bandeira_da_Guin%C3%A9_Bissau_ap%C3%B3s_o_arrear_da_de_Portugal.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Hastear_da_bandeira_da_Guin%C3%A9_Bissau_ap%C3%B3s_o_arrear_da_de_Portugal.jpg/330px-Hastear_da_bandeira_da_Guin%C3%A9_Bissau_ap%C3%B3s_o_arrear_da_de_Portugal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Hastear_da_bandeira_da_Guin%C3%A9_Bissau_ap%C3%B3s_o_arrear_da_de_Portugal.jpg/440px-Hastear_da_bandeira_da_Guin%C3%A9_Bissau_ap%C3%B3s_o_arrear_da_de_Portugal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2381" data-file-height="2149"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hastear_da_bandeira_da_Guin%C3%A9_Bissau_ap%C3%B3s_o_arrear_da_de_Portugal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/PAIGC" class="mw-redirect" title="PAIGC">PAIGC</a> forces raise the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Flag of Guinea-Bissau">flag of Guinea-Bissau</a> in 1974.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Independence was unilaterally declared on 24 September 1973, which is now celebrated as the country's Independence Day, a <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Guinea-Bissau" title="Public holidays in Guinea-Bissau">public holiday</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Recognition became universal following 25 April 1974 socialist-inspired <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">military coup</a> in Portugal, which overthrew Lisbon's <a href="/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Portugal)" title="Estado Novo (Portugal)">Estado Novo regime</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nicolae_Ceau%C8%99escu" title="Nicolae Ceaușescu">Nicolae Ceaușescu</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Romania" title="Socialist Republic of Romania">Romania</a> was the first country to formally recognise Guinea-Bissau and the first to sign agreements with the <a href="/wiki/African_Party_for_the_Independence_of_Guinea_and_Cape_Verde" title="African Party for the Independence of Guinea and Cape Verde">African Party for the Independence of Guinea and Cape Verde</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Cabral" title="Luís Cabral">Luís Cabral</a>, brother of Amílcar and co-founder of PAIGC, was appointed the first <a href="/wiki/President_of_Guinea-Bissau" class="mw-redirect" title="President of Guinea-Bissau">President of Guinea-Bissau</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HISTORY_OF_GUINEA-BISSAU_17-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HISTORY_OF_GUINEA-BISSAU-17">[17]</a></sup> The country was controlled by a revolutionary council until 1984. The first multi-party <a href="/wiki/1994_Guinea-Bissau_general_election" title="1994 Guinea-Bissau general election">elections</a> were held in 1994. An army uprising in May 1998 led to the <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_Civil_War" title="Guinea-Bissau Civil War">Guinea-Bissau Civil War</a> and the president's ousting in June 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Elections were held again in 2000, and <a href="/wiki/Kumba_Ial%C3%A1" title="Kumba Ialá">Kumba Ialá</a> was elected president.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In September 2003, a military coup was conducted. The military arrested Ialá on the charge of being "unable to solve the problems".<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> After being delayed several times, <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_legislative_election,_2004" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinea-Bissau legislative election, 2004">legislative elections</a> were held in March 2004. A <a href="/wiki/Mutiny" title="Mutiny">mutiny</a> of military factions in October 2004 resulted in the death of the head of the armed forces and caused widespread unrest.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="From_Vieira_years_to_present">From Vieira years to present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: From Vieira years to present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In June 2005, presidential elections were held for the first time since the coup that deposed Ialá. Ialá returned as the candidate for the PRS, claiming to be the legitimate president of the country, but the election was won by former president <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Bernardo_Vieira" title="João Bernardo Vieira">João Bernardo Vieira</a>, deposed in the 1999 coup. Vieira beat <a href="/wiki/Malam_Bacai_Sanh%C3%A1" title="Malam Bacai Sanhá">Malam Bacai Sanhá</a> in a run-off election. Sanhá initially refused to concede, claiming that <a href="/wiki/Electoral_fraud" title="Electoral fraud">tampering</a> and electoral fraud occurred in two <a href="/wiki/Constituencies" class="mw-redirect" title="Constituencies">constituencies</a> including the capital, Bissau.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Despite reports of arms entering the country prior to the election and some "disturbances during campaigning", including attacks on government offices by unidentified gunmen, foreign <a href="/wiki/Election_monitoring" title="Election monitoring">election monitors</a> described the <a href="/wiki/2005_Guinea-Bissau_presidential_election" title="2005 Guinea-Bissau presidential election">2005 election</a> overall as "calm and organized".<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Three years later, PAIGC won a strong parliamentary majority, with 67 of 100 seats, in the parliamentary election held in November 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> In November 2008, President Vieira's official residence was attacked by members of the armed forces, killing a guard but leaving the president unharmed.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 2 March 2009, however, Vieira was assassinated by what preliminary reports indicated to be a group of soldiers avenging the death of the head of joint chiefs of staff, General <a href="/wiki/Batista_Tagme_Na_Wai" class="mw-redirect" title="Batista Tagme Na Wai">Batista Tagme Na Wai</a>, who had been killed in an explosion the day before.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Vieira's death did not trigger widespread violence, but there were signs of turmoil in the country, according to the <a href="/wiki/Advocacy_group" title="Advocacy group">advocacy group</a> <a href="/wiki/Swisspeace" title="Swisspeace">Swisspeace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Military leaders in the country pledged to respect the constitutional order of succession. National Assembly Speaker <a href="/wiki/Raimundo_Pereira" title="Raimundo Pereira">Raimundo Pereira</a> was appointed as an interim president until a nationwide <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_presidential_election,_2009" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinea-Bissau presidential election, 2009">election</a> on 28 June 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> It was won by <a href="/wiki/Malam_Bacai_Sanh%C3%A1" title="Malam Bacai Sanhá">Malam Bacai Sanhá</a> of the PAIGC, against <a href="/wiki/Kumba_Ial%C3%A1" title="Kumba Ialá">Kumba Ialá</a> as the presidential candidate of the PRS.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 9 January 2012, President Sanhá died of complications from diabetes, and Pereira was again appointed as an interim president. On the evening of 12 April 2012, members of the country's military staged <a href="/wiki/2012_Guinea-Bissau_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2012 Guinea-Bissau coup d'état">a <i>coup d'état</i></a> and arrested the interim president and a leading presidential candidate.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Former vice chief of staff, General <a href="/wiki/Mamadu_Ture_Kuruma" title="Mamadu Ture Kuruma">Mamadu Ture Kuruma</a>, assumed control of the country in the transitional period and started negotiations with opposition parties.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_M%C3%A1rio_Vaz" title="José Mário Vaz">José Mário Vaz</a> was the President of Guinea-Bissau from 2014 until <a href="/wiki/2019_Guinea-Bissau_presidential_election" title="2019 Guinea-Bissau presidential election">2019 presidential elections</a>. At the end of his term, Vaz became the first elected president to complete his five-year mandate. He lost the 2019 election, however, to <a href="/wiki/Umaro_Sissoco_Embal%C3%B3" title="Umaro Sissoco Embaló">Umaro Sissoco Embaló</a>, who took office in February 2020. Embaló is the first president to be elected without the backing of the PAIGC.<sup id="cite_ref-aa.com.tr_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aa.com.tr-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Politics of Guinea-Bissau">Politics of Guinea-Bissau</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pal%C3%A1cio_Presidencial_em_Bissau_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Pal%C3%A1cio_Presidencial_em_Bissau_%282%29.jpg/220px-Pal%C3%A1cio_Presidencial_em_Bissau_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Pal%C3%A1cio_Presidencial_em_Bissau_%282%29.jpg/330px-Pal%C3%A1cio_Presidencial_em_Bissau_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Pal%C3%A1cio_Presidencial_em_Bissau_%282%29.jpg/440px-Pal%C3%A1cio_Presidencial_em_Bissau_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4518" data-file-height="2422"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pal%C3%A1cio_Presidencial_em_Bissau_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Presidential Palace of Guinea-Bissau
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Fernanda_Nossa,_Guinea-Bissau,_photo_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Fernanda_Nossa%2C_Guinea-Bissau%2C_photo_3.jpg/220px-Fernanda_Nossa%2C_Guinea-Bissau%2C_photo_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Fernanda_Nossa%2C_Guinea-Bissau%2C_photo_3.jpg/330px-Fernanda_Nossa%2C_Guinea-Bissau%2C_photo_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Fernanda_Nossa%2C_Guinea-Bissau%2C_photo_3.jpg/440px-Fernanda_Nossa%2C_Guinea-Bissau%2C_photo_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2992" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Fernanda_Nossa,_Guinea-Bissau,_photo_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Public Order Police officer during a parade in Guinea-Bissau
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Guinea-Bissau is a <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guinea-Bissau_09/03_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guinea-Bissau_09/03-46">[46]</a></sup> In the past, the government had been highly centralized. Multi-party governance was not established until mid-1991.<sup id="cite_ref-Guinea-Bissau_09/03_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guinea-Bissau_09/03-46">[46]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Guinea-Bissau" class="mw-redirect" title="President of Guinea-Bissau">president</a> is the head of state and the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Guinea-Bissau" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister of Guinea-Bissau">prime minister</a> is the head of government. Since 1974, no president had successfully served a full five-year term, until recently when <a href="/wiki/Jose_Mario_Vaz" class="mw-redirect" title="Jose Mario Vaz">Jose Mario Vaz</a> ended his five-year term on 24 June 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-aa.com.tr_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aa.com.tr-44">[44]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At the legislative level, a unicameral <i>Assembleia Nacional Popular</i> (<a href="/wiki/National_People%27s_Assembly_of_Guinea-Bissau" class="mw-redirect" title="National People's Assembly of Guinea-Bissau">National People's Assembly</a>) is made up of 100 members. They are popularly elected from multi-member constituencies to serve a four-year term. The judicial system is headed by a <i>Tribunal Supremo da Justiça</i> (Supreme Court), made up of nine justices appointed by the president; they serve at the pleasure of the president.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The two main political parties are the PAIGC (<a href="/wiki/African_Party_for_the_Independence_of_Guinea_and_Cape_Verde" title="African Party for the Independence of Guinea and Cape Verde">African Party for the Independence of Guinea and Cape Verde</a>) and the PRS (<a href="/wiki/Party_for_Social_Renewal" title="Party for Social Renewal">Party for Social Renewal</a>). There are more than 20 minor parties.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Foreign relations of Guinea-Bissau">Foreign relations of Guinea-Bissau</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Guinea-Bissau follows a nonaligned foreign policy and seeks friendly and cooperative relations with a wide variety of states and organisations.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Guinea-Bissau is a founding member state of the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a> (CPLP), also known as the Lusophone Commonwealth, and international organisation and political association of <a href="/wiki/Lusophone" title="Lusophone">Lusophone</a> nations across four continents, where <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> is an official language.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Military of Guinea-Bissau">Military of Guinea-Bissau</a>
      </div> 
      <p>A 2019 estimate put the size of the Guinea-Bissau Armed Forces at around 4,400 personnel and military spending is less than 2% of GDP .<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018, Guinea-Bissau signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Regions of Guinea-Bissau">Regions of Guinea-Bissau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sectors_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Sectors of Guinea-Bissau">Sectors of Guinea-Bissau</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="floatright">
       <div class="noresize" style="height: 236px; width: 400px; ">
        <map name="ImageMap_4cf4758c03a7774f"><area href="/wiki/Bafat%C3%A1_Region" shape="rect" coords="226,59,289,97" alt="Bafatá Region" title="Bafatá Region"><area href="/wiki/Biombo_Region" shape="rect" coords="274,163,363,183" alt="Biombo Region" title="Biombo Region"><area href="/wiki/Biombo_Region" shape="rect" coords="116,95,132,120" alt="Biombo Region" title="Biombo Region"><area href="/wiki/Bissau_Region" shape="rect" coords="273,188,360,200" alt="Bissau Region" title="Bissau Region"><area href="/wiki/Bissau_Region" shape="rect" coords="138,98,154,117" alt="Bissau Region" title="Bissau Region"><area href="/wiki/Bolama_Region" shape="rect" coords="15,158,85,190" alt="Bolama Region" title="Bolama Region"><area href="/wiki/Cacheu_Region" shape="rect" coords="60,55,136,87" alt="Cacheu Region" title="Cacheu Region"><area href="/wiki/Gab%C3%BA_Region" shape="rect" coords="302,57,356,86" alt="Gabú Region" title="Gabú Region"><area href="/wiki/Oio_Region" shape="rect" coords="168,46,205,80" alt="Oio Region" title="Oio Region"><area href="/wiki/Quinara_Region" shape="rect" coords="273,203,368,223" alt="Quinara Region" title="Quinara Region"><area href="/wiki/Quinara_Region" shape="rect" coords="220,126,238,149" alt="Quinara Region" title="Quinara Region"><area href="/wiki/Tombali_Region" shape="rect" coords="184,166,249,195" alt="Tombali Region" title="Tombali Region"></map>
        <img alt="A clickable map of Guinea-Bissau exhibiting its eight regions and one autonomous sector." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/80/Guinea_Bissau_regions_named.png" decoding="async" width="400" height="236" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="236" usemap="#ImageMap_4cf4758c03a7774f">
        <div style="margin-left: 0px; margin-top: -20px; text-align: left;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Guinea_Bissau_regions_named.png" title="About this image"><img alt="About this image" src="/w/extensions/ImageMap/resources/desc-20.png?15600" style="border: none;"></a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Guinea-Bissau is divided into eight <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Regions of Guinea-Bissau">regions</a> (<i lang="pt" title="Portuguese-language text">regiões</i>) and one <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_entity" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous entity">autonomous</a> <a href="/wiki/Sectors_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Sectors of Guinea-Bissau">sector</a> (<i lang="pt" title="Portuguese-language text">sector autónomo</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> These, in turn, are subdivided into 37 <a href="/wiki/Sectors_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Sectors of Guinea-Bissau">Sectors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guinea-Bissau_Maps_&amp;_Facts_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guinea-Bissau_Maps_&amp;_Facts-53">[53]</a></sup> The regions are:<sup id="cite_ref-Guinea-Bissau_Maps_&amp;_Facts_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guinea-Bissau_Maps_&amp;_Facts-53">[53]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Geography of Guinea-Bissau">Geography of Guinea-Bissau</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lagoa_com_hipop%C3%B3tamos_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Lagoa_com_hipop%C3%B3tamos_01.jpg/230px-Lagoa_com_hipop%C3%B3tamos_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="230" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Lagoa_com_hipop%C3%B3tamos_01.jpg/345px-Lagoa_com_hipop%C3%B3tamos_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Lagoa_com_hipop%C3%B3tamos_01.jpg/460px-Lagoa_com_hipop%C3%B3tamos_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lagoa_com_hipop%C3%B3tamos_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Rare salt water <a href="/wiki/Hippopotamus" title="Hippopotamus">Hippopotamuses</a> in <a href="/wiki/Orango" title="Orango">Orango Island</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:CaravelaIvybeach1p.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/CaravelaIvybeach1p.jpg/230px-CaravelaIvybeach1p.jpg" decoding="async" width="230" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/CaravelaIvybeach1p.jpg/345px-CaravelaIvybeach1p.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/CaravelaIvybeach1p.jpg/460px-CaravelaIvybeach1p.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:CaravelaIvybeach1p.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Caravela, Bissagos Islands
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:20130611-DSC_9018_(9290631541)_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/20130611-DSC_9018_%289290631541%29_%282%29.jpg/230px-20130611-DSC_9018_%289290631541%29_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="230" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/20130611-DSC_9018_%289290631541%29_%282%29.jpg/345px-20130611-DSC_9018_%289290631541%29_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/20130611-DSC_9018_%289290631541%29_%282%29.jpg/460px-20130611-DSC_9018_%289290631541%29_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:20130611-DSC_9018_(9290631541)_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Typical scenery in Guinea-Bissau
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Guinea-Bissau is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> to the north and <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a> to the south and east,<sup id="cite_ref-Guinea-Bissau_Maps_&amp;_Facts_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guinea-Bissau_Maps_&amp;_Facts-53">[53]</a></sup> with the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> to its west.<sup id="cite_ref-Guinea-Bissau_Maps_&amp;_Facts_53-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guinea-Bissau_Maps_&amp;_Facts-53">[53]</a></sup> It lies mostly between latitudes <a href="/wiki/11th_parallel_north" title="11th parallel north">11°</a> and <a href="/wiki/13th_parallel_north" title="13th parallel north">13°N</a> (a small area is south of 11°), and longitudes <a href="/wiki/11th_meridian_west" title="11th meridian west">11°</a> and <a href="/wiki/15th_meridian_west" title="15th meridian west">15°W</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At 36,125 square kilometres (13,948&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-Guinea-Bissau_Maps_&amp;_Facts_53-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guinea-Bissau_Maps_&amp;_Facts-53">[53]</a></sup> the country is larger in size than <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> or <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>. The highest point is 300 metres (984&nbsp;ft). Its terrain is mostly low coastal plains with swamps of the <a href="/wiki/Guinean_mangroves" title="Guinean mangroves">Guinean mangroves</a> rising to the <a href="/wiki/Guinean_forest-savanna_mosaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinean forest-savanna mosaic">Guinean forest-savanna mosaic</a> in the east.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-56">[55]</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a>-like rainy season alternates with periods of hot, dry <a href="/wiki/Harmattan" title="Harmattan">harmattan</a> winds blowing from the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Bijagos_Archipelago" class="mw-redirect" title="Bijagos Archipelago">Bijagos Archipelago</a> lies off of the mainland.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> The country is home to two ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Guinean_forest-savanna_mosaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinean forest-savanna mosaic">Guinean forest-savanna mosaic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guinean_mangroves" title="Guinean mangroves">Guinean mangroves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-58">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Guinea-Bissau" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Guinea-Bissau">Climate of Guinea-Bissau</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Guinea-Bissau is warm all year round with mild temperature fluctuations; it averages 26.3&nbsp;°C (79.3&nbsp;°F). The average rainfall for Bissau is 2,024 millimetres (79.7&nbsp;in), although this is almost entirely accounted for during the rainy season which falls between June and September/October. From December through April, the country experiences drought.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="center">
       <div class="floatnone">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Climate_diagram_of_Bissau,_Guinea-Bissau.svg" class="image"><img alt="Climate diagram of Bissau, Guinea-Bissau.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Climate_diagram_of_Bissau%2C_Guinea-Bissau.svg/600px-Climate_diagram_of_Bissau%2C_Guinea-Bissau.svg.png" decoding="async" width="600" height="302" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Climate_diagram_of_Bissau%2C_Guinea-Bissau.svg/900px-Climate_diagram_of_Bissau%2C_Guinea-Bissau.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Climate_diagram_of_Bissau%2C_Guinea-Bissau.svg/1200px-Climate_diagram_of_Bissau%2C_Guinea-Bissau.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1263" data-file-height="635"></a>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_problems">Environmental problems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Environmental problems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Severe environmental problems include <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soil_erosion" title="Soil erosion">soil erosion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Overgrazing" title="Overgrazing">overgrazing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Overfishing" title="Overfishing">overfishing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-56">[55]</a></sup> Guinea-Bissau had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 5.7/10, ranking it 97th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-60">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Economy of Guinea-Bissau">Economy of Guinea-Bissau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mining_industry_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Mining industry of Guinea-Bissau">Mining industry of Guinea-Bissau</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Banco_Centra_Da_Guine_Bissau.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Banco_Centra_Da_Guine_Bissau.JPG/220px-Banco_Centra_Da_Guine_Bissau.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Banco_Centra_Da_Guine_Bissau.JPG/330px-Banco_Centra_Da_Guine_Bissau.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Banco_Centra_Da_Guine_Bissau.JPG/440px-Banco_Centra_Da_Guine_Bissau.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1319" data-file-height="956"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Banco_Centra_Da_Guine_Bissau.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Seat of the Central Bank of Guinea-Bissau
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Posto_Galp_em_S%C3%A3o_Domingos,_Guin%C3%A9_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Posto_Galp_em_S%C3%A3o_Domingos%2C_Guin%C3%A9_%281%29.jpg/220px-Posto_Galp_em_S%C3%A3o_Domingos%2C_Guin%C3%A9_%281%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Posto_Galp_em_S%C3%A3o_Domingos%2C_Guin%C3%A9_%281%29.jpg/330px-Posto_Galp_em_S%C3%A3o_Domingos%2C_Guin%C3%A9_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Posto_Galp_em_S%C3%A3o_Domingos%2C_Guin%C3%A9_%281%29.jpg/440px-Posto_Galp_em_S%C3%A3o_Domingos%2C_Guin%C3%A9_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Posto_Galp_em_S%C3%A3o_Domingos,_Guin%C3%A9_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Petrol station in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Domingos_(Guinea-Bissau)" title="São Domingos (Guinea-Bissau)">São Domingos</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Guinea-Bissau's <a href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP per capita">GDP per capita</a> is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">lowest in the world</a>, and its <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">lowest on earth</a>. More than two-thirds of the population lives below the poverty line.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> The economy depends mainly on agriculture; fish, <a href="/wiki/Cashew_nuts" class="mw-redirect" title="Cashew nuts">cashew nuts</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bambara_groundnut" class="mw-redirect" title="Bambara groundnut">ground nuts</a> are its major exports.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>A long period of political instability has resulted in depressed economic activity, deteriorating social conditions, and increased macroeconomic imbalances. It takes longer on average to register a new business in Guinea-Bissau (233 days or about 33 weeks) than in any other country in the world except <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Guinea-Bissau has started to show some economic advances after a pact of stability was signed by the main political parties of the country, leading to an <a href="/wiki/IMF" class="mw-redirect" title="IMF">IMF</a>-backed structural reform program.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> The key challenges for the country in the period ahead are to achieve fiscal discipline, rebuild public administration, improve the economic climate for private investment, and promote economic diversification. After the country became independent from Portugal in 1974 due to the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Colonial_War" title="Portuguese Colonial War">Portuguese Colonial War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a>, the rapid exodus of the Portuguese civilian, military, and political authorities resulted in considerable damage to the country's economic infrastructure, <a href="/wiki/Social_order" title="Social order">social order</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Standard_of_living" title="Standard of living">standard of living</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>After several years of economic downturn and political instability, in 1997, Guinea-Bissau entered the <a href="/wiki/CFA_franc" title="CFA franc">CFA franc</a> monetary system, bringing about some internal monetary stability.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> The civil war that took place in 1998 and 1999, and a military coup in September 2003 again disrupted economic activity, leaving a substantial part of the economic and social infrastructure in ruins and intensifying the already widespread poverty. Following the parliamentary elections in March 2004 and presidential elections in July 2005, the country is trying to recover from the long period of instability, despite a still-fragile political situation.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Beginning around 2005, drug traffickers based in Latin America began to use Guinea-Bissau, along with several neighbouring West African nations, as a transshipment point to Europe for <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> The nation was described by a United Nations official as being at risk for becoming a "<a href="/wiki/Narco-state" title="Narco-state">narco-state</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-drugs_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drugs-68">[67]</a></sup> The government and the military have done little to stop drug trafficking, which increased after the <a href="/wiki/2012_Guinea-Bissau_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2012 Guinea-Bissau coup d'état">2012 coup d'état</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> The government of Guinea-Bissau continues to be ravaged by illegal drug distribution, according to The Week magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> Guinea-Bissau is a member of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Organisation_for_the_Harmonisation_of_Business_Law_in_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Organisation for the Harmonisation of Business Law in Africa (page does not exist)">Organisation for the Harmonisation of Business Law in Africa</a> (<a href="/wiki/OHADA" title="OHADA">OHADA</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-ohada.com_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohada.com-71">[70]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Demographics of Guinea-Bissau">Demographics of Guinea-Bissau</a>
      </div> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:333px;max-width:333px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:177px;max-width:177px">

          </div>

        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">

          (Left) Guinea-Bissau's population between 1961 and 2003. (Right) Guinea-Bissau's <a href="/wiki/Population_pyramid" title="Population pyramid">population pyramid</a>, 2005. In 2010, 41.3% of Guinea-Bissau's population were aged under 15.<sup id="cite_ref-WPP_2010_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WPP_2010-72">[71]</a></sup>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the 2019 revision of the World Population Prospects<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-4">[4]</a></sup>, Guinea-Bissau's population was 1,874,303 in 2018, compared to 518,000 in 1950. The proportion of the population below the age of 15 in 2010 was 41.3%, 55.4% were aged between 15 and 65 years of age, while 3.3% were aged 65 years or older.<sup id="cite_ref-WPP_2010_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WPP_2010-72">[71]</a></sup> </p>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Geographic_location_of_Guinea-Bissau_and_present-day_settlement_pattern_of_the_ethnic_groups.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Geographic_location_of_Guinea-Bissau_and_present-day_settlement_pattern_of_the_ethnic_groups.jpg/330px-Geographic_location_of_Guinea-Bissau_and_present-day_settlement_pattern_of_the_ethnic_groups.jpg" decoding="async" width="330" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Geographic_location_of_Guinea-Bissau_and_present-day_settlement_pattern_of_the_ethnic_groups.jpg/495px-Geographic_location_of_Guinea-Bissau_and_present-day_settlement_pattern_of_the_ethnic_groups.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Geographic_location_of_Guinea-Bissau_and_present-day_settlement_pattern_of_the_ethnic_groups.jpg/660px-Geographic_location_of_Guinea-Bissau_and_present-day_settlement_pattern_of_the_ethnic_groups.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="526"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Geographic_location_of_Guinea-Bissau_and_present-day_settlement_pattern_of_the_ethnic_groups.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Guinea-Bissau present-day settlement pattern of the ethnic groups
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The population of Guinea-Bissau is ethnically diverse and has many distinct languages, customs, and social structures.<sup id="cite_ref-Guinea-Bissau_09/03_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guinea-Bissau_09/03-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Bissau-Guineans can be divided into the following ethnic groups:<sup id="cite_ref-Guinea-Bissau_09/03_46-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guinea-Bissau_09/03-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fula</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mandinka_language" title="Mandinka language">Mandinka</a>-speaking people, who comprise the largest portion of the population and are concentrated in the north and northeast;<sup id="cite_ref-Guinea-Bissau_09/03_46-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guinea-Bissau_09/03-46">[46]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Balanta_people" title="Balanta people">Balanta</a> and Papel people, who live in the southern coastal regions;<sup id="cite_ref-Guinea-Bissau_09/03_46-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guinea-Bissau_09/03-46">[46]</a></sup> and</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Manjak_people" title="Manjak people">Manjaco</a> and Mancanha, who occupy the central and northern coastal areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Guinea-Bissau_09/03_46-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guinea-Bissau_09/03-46">[46]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Most of the remainder are <i><a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestiços</a></i> of mixed <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> and African descent.<sup id="cite_ref-cciei.org_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cciei.org-74">[73]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Portuguese natives comprise a very small percentage of Bissau-Guineans.<sup id="cite_ref-cciei.org_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cciei.org-74">[73]</a></sup> After Guinea-Bissau gained independence, most of the Portuguese nationals left the country. The country has a tiny <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Chinese</a> population.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> These include traders and merchants of mixed Portuguese and Chinese ancestry from the former Asian <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a> colony of <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cciei.org_74-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cciei.org-74">[73]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_cities">Major cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Major cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;">

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Languages of Guinea-Bissau">Languages of Guinea-Bissau</a>

      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Voter_education_for_guinea_bissau_elections_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Voter_education_for_guinea_bissau_elections_2008.jpg/220px-Voter_education_for_guinea_bissau_elections_2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Voter_education_for_guinea_bissau_elections_2008.jpg/330px-Voter_education_for_guinea_bissau_elections_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Voter_education_for_guinea_bissau_elections_2008.jpg/440px-Voter_education_for_guinea_bissau_elections_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Voter_education_for_guinea_bissau_elections_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Voter education posters in <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_Creole" title="Guinea-Bissau Creole">Kriol</a> for <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_legislative_election,_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinea-Bissau legislative election, 2008">Guinea-Bissau legislative election, 2008</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biombo_Region" title="Biombo Region">Biombo Region</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Despite being a small country Guinea-Bissau has several ethnic groups which are very distinct from each other, with their own cultures and languages. This is due to Guinea-Bissau being a refugee and migration territory within Africa. Colonisation and racial intermixing brought Portuguese and the Portuguese creole known as <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_Creole" title="Guinea-Bissau Creole">Kriol</a> or <i>crioulo</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-barbosa_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-barbosa-77">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although the only official language of Guinea-Bissau since independence, Standard <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> is spoken mostly as a second language, with few native speakers and its use is often confined to the intellectual and political elites. It is the language of government and national communication as a legacy of colonial rule. Schooling from the primary to tertiary levels is conducted in Portuguese, although only 67% of children have access to any formal education. Data suggests that the number of Portuguese speakers ranges from 11 to 15%.<sup id="cite_ref-cciei.org_74-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cciei.org-74">[73]</a></sup> In the latest census (2009) 27.1% of the population claimed to speak non-creole Portuguese (46.3% of city dwellers and 14.7% of the rural population, respectively).<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> Portuguese creole is spoken by 44% of the population and is effectively the lingua franca among distinct groups for most of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-cciei.org_74-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cciei.org-74">[73]</a></sup> Creole's usage is still expanding, and it is understood by the vast majority of the population. However, <a href="/wiki/Decreolisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Decreolisation">decreolisation</a> processes are occurring, due to undergoing interference from Standard Portuguese and the creole forms a continuum of varieties with the standard language, the most distant are <a href="/wiki/Basilect" class="mw-redirect" title="Basilect">basilects</a> and the closer ones, <a href="/wiki/Acrolect" class="mw-redirect" title="Acrolect">acrolects</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Post-creole_continuum" title="Post-creole continuum">post-creole continuum</a> exists in Guinea-Bissau and crioulo 'leve' ('soft' creole) variety being closer to the Portuguese-language norm.<sup id="cite_ref-barbosa_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-barbosa-77">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The remaining rural population speaks a variety of native African languages unique to each ethnicity: <a href="/wiki/Fula_language" title="Fula language">Fula</a> (16%), <a href="/wiki/Balanta_language" title="Balanta language">Balanta</a> (14%), <a href="/wiki/Mandinka_language" title="Mandinka language">Mandinka</a> (7%), <a href="/wiki/Manjak_language" title="Manjak language">Manjak</a> (5%), Papel (3%), Felupe (1%), Beafada (0.7%), Bijagó (0.3%), and Nalu (0.1%), which form the ethnic African languages spoken by the population.<sup id="cite_ref-barbosa_77-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-barbosa-77">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> Most Portuguese and Mestiços speakers also have one of the African languages and Kriol as additional languages. Ethnic African languages are not discouraged, in any situation, despite their lower prestige. These languages are the link between individuals of the same ethnic background and daily used in villages, between neighbours or friends, traditional and religious ceremonies, and also used in contact between the urban and rural populations. However, none of these languages are dominant in Guinea-Bissau.<sup id="cite_ref-barbosa_77-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-barbosa-77">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>French is taught as a foreign language in schools, because Guinea-Bissau is surrounded by French-speaking nations.<sup id="cite_ref-cciei.org_74-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cciei.org-74">[73]</a></sup> Guinea-Bissau is a full member of the <a href="/wiki/Francophonie" class="mw-redirect" title="Francophonie">Francophonie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Guinea-Bissau" title="Religion in Guinea-Bissau">Religion in Guinea-Bissau</a>
