      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bafata1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Bafata1.jpg/220px-Bafata1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Bafata1.jpg/330px-Bafata1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Bafata1.jpg/440px-Bafata1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bafata1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Men in Islamic garb, <a href="/wiki/Bafat%C3%A1" title="Bafatá">Bafatá</a>, Guinea-Bissau
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There are conflicting reports of religious demographics. The CIA World Factbook has a 2008 estimate of 45.1% Muslim, 22.1% Christian, 14.9% animist, 2% none, and 15.9% unspecified.<sup id="cite_ref-cia-religion_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-religion-12">[12]</a></sup> In 2010, a Pew Research survey found that the primary affiliation of the population is 45.1% Muslim and 19.7% Christian, with 30.9% Folk religion and 4.3 for other affiliations.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pew_Africa_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew_Africa-81">[80]</a></sup> A 2015 Pew-Templeton study claims a different distribution in 2010, consisting of 45.1% Muslim, 30.9% folk religions, 19.7% Christians, and 4.3% unaffiliated.<sup id="cite_ref-pewtemp-religion_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pewtemp-religion-82">[81]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to another Pew report, concerning religious identity among Muslims, it was determined that in Guinea-Bissau there is no prevailing sectarian identity. Under this same category were other Sub-Saharan countries like Tanzania, Uganda, Liberia, Nigeria and Cameroon. Other nations around the world claimed to be either predominantly Just Muslim, Mix of Sunni and Shia, or predominantly Sunni (pg. 30).<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> This Pew research also stated that countries in this specific study that declared to not have any clear dominant sectarian identity were mostly concentrated in Sub-Saharan Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> Another Pew report, <i>The Future of World Religions</i>, predicts that from 2010 to 2050 Islam will increase its percent of the population in Guinea-Bissau.<sup id="cite_ref-pewtemp-religion_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pewtemp-religion-82">[81]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Many residents practice <a href="/wiki/Religious_syncretism" title="Religious syncretism">syncretic</a> forms of Islamic and Christian faiths, combining their practices with traditional African beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-56">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EB_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-85">[84]</a></sup> Muslims dominate the north and east, while Christians dominate the south and coastal regions. The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> claims most of the Christian community.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Guinea-Bissau" title="Health in Guinea-Bissau">Health in Guinea-Bissau</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Guinea-Bissau" title="Education in Guinea-Bissau">Education in Guinea-Bissau</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Universidade_Lus%C3%B3fona,_Bissau.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Universidade_Lus%C3%B3fona%2C_Bissau.jpg/200px-Universidade_Lus%C3%B3fona%2C_Bissau.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="113" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Universidade_Lus%C3%B3fona%2C_Bissau.jpg/300px-Universidade_Lus%C3%B3fona%2C_Bissau.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Universidade_Lus%C3%B3fona%2C_Bissau.jpg/400px-Universidade_Lus%C3%B3fona%2C_Bissau.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="2592"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Ungdomsbiblioteket_Bissau.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Ungdomsbiblioteket_Bissau.jpg/200px-Ungdomsbiblioteket_Bissau.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Ungdomsbiblioteket_Bissau.jpg/300px-Ungdomsbiblioteket_Bissau.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Ungdomsbiblioteket_Bissau.jpg/400px-Ungdomsbiblioteket_Bissau.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/Universidade_Lus%C3%B3fona" title="Universidade Lusófona">Universidade Lusófona</a> of Bissau (up). Students at Biblioteca Jovem, Bairro da Ajuda, in Guinea-Bissau. (down)
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Education is compulsory from the age of 7 to 13.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> Pre-school education for children between three and six years of age is optional and in its early stages. There are five levels of education: pre-school, elemental and complementary basic education, general and complementary secondary education, general secondary education, technical and professional teaching, and higher education (university and non-universities). Basic education is under reform, and now forms a single cycle, comprising 6 years of education. Secondary education is widely available and there are two cycles (7th to 9th <i>classe</i> and 10th to 11th <i>classe</i>). Professional education in public institutions is nonoperational, however private school offerings opened, including the <i>Centro de Formação São João Bosco</i> (since 2004) and the <i>Centro de Formação Luís Inácio Lula da Silva</i> (since 2011).<sup id="cite_ref-barbosa_77-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-barbosa-77">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Higher education is limited and most prefer to be educated abroad, with students preferring to enroll in Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-barbosa_77-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-barbosa-77">[76]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Guinea-Bissau" title="List of universities in Guinea-Bissau">number of universities</a>, to which an institutionally autonomous Faculty of Law as well as a Faculty of Medicine<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Child_labor" class="mw-redirect" title="Child labor">Child labor</a> is very common.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-89">[88]</a></sup> The enrollment of boys is higher than that of girls. In 1998, the gross primary enrollment rate was 53.5%, with higher enrollment ratio for males (67.7%) compared to females (40%).<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-89">[88]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Non-formal education is centered on community schools and the teaching of adults.<sup id="cite_ref-barbosa_77-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-barbosa-77">[76]</a></sup> In 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Literacy rate">literacy rate</a> was estimated at 55.3% (68.9% male, and 42.1% female).<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conflicts">Conflicts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Conflicts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Usually, the many different ethnic groups in Guinea-Bissau coexist peacefully, but when conflicts do erupt, they tend to revolve around access to land.<sup id="cite_ref-D+C_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D+C-91">[90]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Guinea-Bissau" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Guinea-Bissau">Media of Guinea-Bissau</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Music of Guinea-Bissau">Music of Guinea-Bissau</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The music of Guinea-Bissau is usually associated with the <a href="/wiki/Polyrhythm" title="Polyrhythm">polyrhythmic</a> <a href="/wiki/Gumbe" title="Gumbe">gumbe</a> <a href="/wiki/Musical_genre" class="mw-redirect" title="Musical genre">genre</a>, the country's primary musical export. However, civil unrest and other factors have combined over the years to keep gumbe, and other genres, out of mainstream audiences, even in generally syncretist African countries.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Cabasa" title="Cabasa">cabasa</a> is the primary <a href="/wiki/Musical_instrument" title="Musical instrument">musical instrument</a> of Guinea-Bissau,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> and is used in extremely swift and rhythmically complex <a href="/wiki/Dance_music" title="Dance music">dance music</a>. Lyrics are almost always in <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_Creole" title="Guinea-Bissau Creole">Guinea-Bissau Creole</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">creole language</a>, and are often humorous and topical, revolving around current events and controversies.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The word <i>gumbe</i> is sometimes used generically, to refer to any music of the country, although it most specifically refers to a unique style that fuses about ten of the country's <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk music</a> traditions.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Music of Guinea-Bissau">Tina and tinga</a> are other popular genres, while extent folk traditions include ceremonial music used in funerals, <a href="/wiki/Initiation" title="Initiation">initiations</a>, and other rituals, as well as <a href="/wiki/Balanta_people" title="Balanta people">Balanta</a> brosca and kussundé, <a href="/wiki/Mandinka_people" title="Mandinka people">Mandinga</a> djambadon, and the kundere sound of the <a href="/wiki/Bissagos_Islands" title="Bissagos Islands">Bissagos Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Guinea-Bissau" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuisine of Guinea-Bissau">Cuisine of Guinea-Bissau</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Rice is a staple in the diet of residents near the coast and millet a staple in the interior. Fruits and vegetables are commonly eaten along with <a href="/wiki/Cereal_grain" class="mw-redirect" title="Cereal grain">cereal grains</a>. The Portuguese encouraged <a href="/wiki/Peanut" title="Peanut">peanut</a> production. <a href="/wiki/Vigna_subterranea" title="Vigna subterranea">Vigna subterranea</a> (Bambara groundnut) and <a href="/wiki/Macrotyloma_geocarpum" title="Macrotyloma geocarpum">Macrotyloma geocarpum</a> (Hausa groundnut) are also grown. <a href="/wiki/Black-eyed_pea" title="Black-eyed pea">Black-eyed peas</a> are also part of the diet. <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">Palm oil</a> is harvested.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Common dishes include <a href="/wiki/Soup" title="Soup">soups</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stew" title="Stew">stews</a>. Common ingredients include <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">sweet potato</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a>, onion, tomato, and <a href="/wiki/Cooking_banana" title="Cooking banana">plantain</a>. Spices, peppers, and chilis are used in cooking, including <a href="/wiki/Aframomum_melegueta" title="Aframomum melegueta">Aframomum melegueta</a> seeds (Guinea pepper).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film">Film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Flora_Gomes" title="Flora Gomes">Flora Gomes</a> is an internationally renowned film director; his most famous film is <i><a href="/wiki/Nha_Fala" class="mw-redirect" title="Nha Fala">Nha Fala</a></i> (English: <span lang="en">My Voice</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> Gomes's <i><a href="/wiki/Mortu_Nega" title="Mortu Nega">Mortu Nega</a></i> (<i>Death Denied</i>) (1988)<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> was the first fiction film and the second feature film ever made in Guinea-Bissau. (The first feature film was <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=N%E2%80%99tturudu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="N’tturudu (page does not exist)">N’tturudu</a></i>, by director <a href="/w/index.php?title=Umban_u%E2%80%99Kest&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Umban u’Kest (page does not exist)">Umban u’Kest</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&nbsp;[<a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umba%C3%B1_U_Kset" class="extiw" title="fr:Umbañ U Kset">fr</a>]</span> in 1987.) At <a href="/wiki/FESPACO" class="mw-redirect" title="FESPACO">FESPACO</a> 1989, <i>Mortu Nega</i> won the prestigious Oumarou Ganda Prize. In 1992, Gomes directed <i><a href="/wiki/Udju_Azul_di_Yonta" class="mw-redirect" title="Udju Azul di Yonta">Udju Azul di Yonta</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> which was screened in the <a href="/wiki/Un_Certain_Regard" title="Un Certain Regard">Un Certain Regard</a> section at the <a href="/wiki/1992_Cannes_Film_Festival" title="1992 Cannes Film Festival">1992 Cannes Film Festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-festival-cannes.com_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-festival-cannes.com-100">[99]</a></sup> Gomes has also served on the boards of many Africa-centric film festivals.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> The actress <a href="/wiki/Babetida_Sadjo" title="Babetida Sadjo">Babetida Sadjo</a> was born in <a href="/wiki/Bafat%C3%A1" title="Bafatá">Bafatá</a>, Guinea-Bissau.<sup id="cite_ref-rtbf_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rtbf-102">[101]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Football is the most popular sport in Guinea-Bissau. The <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_national_football_team" title="Guinea-Bissau national football team">Guinea-Bissau national football team</a> is controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Football_Federation_of_Guinea-Bissau" title="Football Federation of Guinea-Bissau">Federação de Futebol da Guiné-Bissau</a>. They are a member of the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_African_Football" title="Confederation of African Football">Confederation of African Football</a> (CAF) and FIFA. Other football clubs include <a href="/wiki/Desportivo_Quelele" title="Desportivo Quelele">Desportivo Quelele</a>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Catacumba" title="FC Catacumba">FC Catacumba</a>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Catacumba_Sao_Domingos" class="mw-redirect" title="FC Catacumba Sao Domingos">FC Catacumba São Domingos</a>, FC Cupelaoo Gabu, <a href="/wiki/FC_Djaraf" title="FC Djaraf">FC Djaraf</a>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Prabis" title="FC Prabis">FC Prabis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/FC_Babaque" title="FC Babaque">FC Babaque</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Well-known football players who were born in Guinea-Bissau include: </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Ansu_Fati" title="Ansu Fati">Ansu Fati</a> (Bissau, 2002), has been playing for <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a>, Spain since 2019. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Bruma_(footballer)" title="Bruma (footballer)">Bruma</a> (Bissau, 1994), has been playing for <a href="/wiki/PSV_Eindhoven" title="PSV Eindhoven">PSV Eindhoven</a>, The Netherlands since 2019. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Eder_(Portuguese_footballer)" title="Eder (Portuguese footballer)">Éderzito António Macedo Lopes</a> (Éder) (Bissau, 1987), has been playing for <a href="/wiki/Lokomotiv_Moscow" class="mw-redirect" title="Lokomotiv Moscow">Lokomotiv Moscow</a>, Russia since 2018. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Mama_Samba_Bald%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Mama Samba Baldé">Mama Samba Baldé</a> (Bissau 1995), has been playing for <a href="/wiki/Dijon_FCO" title="Dijon FCO">Dijon FCO</a>, France since 2019. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Joelson_Fernandes" title="Joelson Fernandes">Joelson Fernandes</a> (Bissau, 2014) has been playing for <a href="/wiki/Sporting_Lisbon" class="mw-redirect" title="Sporting Lisbon">Sporting Lisbon</a>, Portugal since 2020. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Danilo_Lu%C3%ADs_H%C3%A9lio_Pereira" class="mw-redirect" title="Danilo Luís Hélio Pereira">Danilo Luís Hélio Pereira</a> (Danilo) (Bissau, 1991) has been playing for <a href="/wiki/Paris_Saint_Germain" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris Saint Germain">Paris Saint Germain</a>, France since 2020. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Carlos_Embal%C3%B3" title="Carlos Embaló">Carlos Embaló</a> (Bissau, 1994) has been playing for <a href="/wiki/KAS_Eupen" class="mw-redirect" title="KAS Eupen">KAS Eupen</a>, Belgium since 2019. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Toni_Silva" title="Toni Silva">Toni Brito Silva Sá (Toni Silva)</a> (Bissau, 1993) has been playing for <a href="/wiki/FC_Taraz" title="FC Taraz">FC Taraz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazachstan" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazachstan">Kazachstan</a> since February 2020. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Jorginho_(footballer,_born_1995)" title="Jorginho (footballer, born 1995)">Jorge Fernando Barbosa Intima</a>, known as Jorginho, (Bissau, 1995) has been playing for <a href="/wiki/Wadi_Degla_SC" title="Wadi Degla SC">Wadi Degla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, since November 2020. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea-Bissau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
